Snippets from the "Council of State" in Chongqing - Transmitted from Macau on January 29th

According to reports, the first session of the third "Council of State" in Chongqing convened on October 22nd of the 31st year [of the Republic, i.e., 1942], lasting for ten days. Looking back today, although it feels like reviewing yesterday's news, these scattered glimpses still offer a lingering sense of interest.

Councilor Gu Jiegang, upon arriving at seat number 195, searched anxiously for his books, only to later realize, with Councilor Wang Yinzhi's arrival, that it was Wang's seat. His own seat was actually in the same row, but in the first three rows. The confusion and mistake caused him great alarm, and the two couldn't help but laugh.

Many councilors greeted each other in the morning with the question, "Where did you hide during last night's air raid alert?"

After the afternoon session, Councilors Yang Duanliu and Chen Yuan, unable to board a vehicle, had to walk back to their residence.

Gu Jiegang encountered Huang Yanpei and repeatedly greeted him with "Congratulations, congratulations," to which Huang responded with a smile.

Councilor Hadeer, from Xinjiang, could barely speak Mandarin but was fluent in English and French, having studied in Syria.

Female Councilor Tang Guozhen actively engaged inside and outside the meeting venue during the ten-minute break, seeking co-signatures for her proposal. One of the proposals concerned increasing salaries for university professors. ("University professors are even worse off than primary school teachers," was a point of great concern for Councilor Tang.)

Chen Lifu, when discussing the lives of primary school teachers, stated that their monthly salary was about 62 yuan, plus two dou of rice (also worth 62 yuan), for a total monthly income of 124 yuan.

Female Councilor Zhang Bangzhen inquired about the lack of teachers and unavailable textbooks. Tong Guanxian, Peng Ge and Chen inquired about student malnutrition and students carrying firearms in schools and engaging in unlawful behavior. Mr. Chen prepared to respond to all these inquiries in writing.

In one educational inquiry regarding the low level of primary school teachers, the following incident was mentioned: A certain county magistrate, while on inspection tour, found that the local primary school teacher, in an attempt to show the people's welcome to the magistrate, posted slogans everywhere. One of them read "The county magistrate's spirit never dies," causing laughter throughout the hall.

Wei Zhiguang, the director of the central labor administration, planned to propose a bill for "special medical expenses for civil servants and staff" to the assembly. As Wei said, "Who can afford to get sick these days? If the government doesn't come up with some solutions for these people within a reasonable scope, they will just have to wait to die when they get sick!"

A proposal suggesting that students must read the "Great Learning," the "Doctrine of the Mean," and the "Analects" and that universities should establish institutes for studying classical texts sparked heated debate. The initial review stated "reserved", Councilor Liu Hengjing agreed with the reservation, stating as a reason that "reading old books will only create fake antiques." Councilor Peng Yunyi asked, "Isn't the "Fuxing Academy" already studying classical texts?" Councilor Tao Xuan, addressing Councilor Liu Hengjing's point of view, stated, "China needs personality training, China should promote its inherent moral education, and reading old books will not turn people into antiques." Councilor Li Zhongxiang, Councilor Jiang Yiping, and Councilor Chu Fucheng all expressed agreement with and opposition to the opinions. The result was that the proposition to make "The Great Learning", "The Doctrine of the Mean" and "The Analects" compulsory extracurricular reading was passed and sent to the government for adoption and implementation.

After the proposal to promote reading the classics was passed, Councilor Wang Hanzhu suddenly stood up and declared, "Even if you revoke my qualification as a councilor, I must speak." He argued that the word "compulsory" should not be added to "extracurricular." However, after others informed him that it was possible to add "compulsory" to "extracurricular," Wang remained silent.

Councilors also engaged in a lively discussion regarding the loan issue for students from war zones. The proposer stated, "Prisoners in jail have all their living expenses covered by the state. Even before they are executed, they are given a full meal. Why should students from war zones have their loans canceled simply because of poor academic performance, thus cutting off their livelihood?" The listeners were moved by this.

Regarding Councilor Luo Heng's proposal to abolish the Relief and Rehabilitation Committee, Councilor Chou Ao strongly argued against it. Luo stood up and gave a very long explanation, pointing out as many as fourteen shortcomings of the Relief and Rehabilitation Committee, and stating that anyone who argued against this proposal was protecting the committee. Councilor Tao Xuan, one of those who opposed Luo's proposal, specifically reminded everyone, "Don't let Luo's arguments lock up our mouths like a lock." Councilor Huang Yuren jokingly said, "I'm afraid people will say I'm being locked up by a lock, so I have to speak. My opinion is to maintain the review opinion." For a while, Councilor Jiang Yiping, Councilor Kong Geng, and Councilor Wang Liming all remained silent. The result was that the proposal was revised and sent to the government for investigation and action.

Among the councilors was a one-legged gentleman, Zhang Tong, and a one-armed gentleman, Liang Shangdong.

The various review committees at this session were extremely busy, especially the fourth and fifth groups. The fourth review committee (finance, economy, transportation) even worked overtime until the 30th of the month to deal with various important cases. All the councilors felt "overwhelmed." At each conference, the second review committee (international diplomacy) was the most idle, hence the nickname "lazy group." However, this time it had twelve proposals to review, but it finished in less than six hours.

The trend of councilors freely leaving the session had not diminished. Some councilors sitting in the back row would often move to the spectator seats to chat with guests.

Councilor Chen Yiyun was greatly dissatisfied upon hearing reports that in war zones, married women who had been separated from their husbands for five years could remarry without the government recognizing it as bigamy. He inquired with Xie Guansheng, the Minister of Judicial Administration, who replied in writing, stating that there was no such thing.

It was reported that the Council of State received a total of 250 proposals, 92 of which concerned economic and financial matters, including 27 related to price issues, reflecting the nationwide concern about prices.

Current Stage of the German-Soviet War - The Battle for Rostov Reaches a Critical Juncture

Everywhere on the bitterly cold German-Soviet winter front, covered in frost and snow, fierce battles are unfolding, attracting significant attention. The German authorities also acknowledge the gravity of the situation and are urging their citizens to develop a new awareness. The current stage of the German-Soviet war is observed by synthesizing reports from various locations.

Along the vast German-Soviet front, stretching from the Leningrad area in the north to the North Caucasus in the south, the Soviet side has launched a counteroffensive despite suffering heavy losses. Last autumn, as the battle for Stalingrad intensified, the Soviet high command appointed Marshal Zhukov (then a Corps General), commander of the Central Front, as the supreme commander. He led fifty reserve divisions, awaiting an opportunity to strike the German rear during the winter. The Germans were aware of this plan from the beginning and had the Sixth Army and a part of the Romanian army build strong fortifications in the occupied area of Stalingrad, demonstrating their determination to fight resolutely on the Volga River.

On November 19th, the Soviet forces, which had been waiting for this moment, launched their operation from the northwest and southwest of Stalingrad, opening the prelude to the winter campaign in the area between the Volga and Don rivers. Subsequently, on November 25th, in the Central Front's Garinine northwest of Elziv, Toropetz, and Verikiel, on December 16th in the Bokocher, Nobelier, and Garitope regions of the middle Don, and in January in the Mozdok and Nari Zhetge regions of the central North Caucasus, and in the Leningrad eastern Ladojia Southern Lake regions, the Soviet forces took counteroffensive postures. In the fierce battles between the attacking and defending armies, progress was made in the southern war zone, with the major battlefield having a radius of 180 to 80 kilometers, centered on Voroshilov and Rostov.

The direction of the Soviet counteroffensive in this southern war zone was, in the northernmost region near Voronezh, commanded by General Gorlikov, and aimed at capturing Voronezh and advancing towards Kharkiv. In the middle reaches of the Don River, Lieutenant General Rokossovsky's troops crossed the Don River, with one part advancing from Staire Lisk towards the north of Voroshilovgrad, and another part heading south along the Moscow-Rostov railway through Millerovo to Minsk Leovsky, advancing towards the north of Rostov. Another group came out of the Kutsirini Gov region from the southwest of Stalingrad along the Stalingrad, Tsiolek, and Novo Rossiysk railway. General Airmenko's right-wing forces concentrated near the point where the Don and Donets rivers diverge, near Konstantinov Pusko, keeping an eye on the east of Rostov. The front line advanced towards Rostov along the north bank of the Manuichi Canal, and the left wing advanced west from Salisk, echoing the forces advancing north from the North Caucasus to attack Tsiolek, a key point in the south of Rostov.

Thus, what is the target of the Soviet counteroffensive on the southern front? First, Rostov, to cut off the connection between the German forces in the North Caucasus and eastern Ukraine, and to encircle and recapture the Donbas mining and industrial area from both the north and south, and to retake Kharkiv. Voronezh was first captured by the German forces in July last year when they began their summer offensive, and from there they controlled the important areas of Kursk and Kharkiv in the west.

The Soviet army took advantage of the opportunity of the slightly reduced severity of the winter to use tank groups as the main force of the attack, launching successive attacks on the German positions with tenacious attacks. Marshal Timoshenko, the loser of the southern front, was replaced by the young General Vatutin as commander, who, together with Marshal Zhukov, commanded 800,000 troops in a major counteroffensive.

The scale of the counteroffensive on the northern front in the central region was smaller than that in the south, but it regained the Hilleselipurgo and Veriki-Erji districts at the southern end of Lake Latga. The flank operations of the southern war front gradually became deadlocked due to the German counteroffensive after transferring to a new position in mid-January. However, the Soviet Union's propaganda that the attempt to regain Hilleselipurgo was intended to relieve Leningrad.

The German forces on the southern war front, led by Field Marshal Manstein, the brave conqueror of Sevastopol, replacing Field Marshal Bock, conducted a flexible retreat and defensive deployment, forming a strong new trapezoidal position facing the Soviet army in the rear of the war front, owing to last winter's defensive battles. Because the extension of the front line was quite vast, the front line and the rear had to maintain a very long supply line, which was obviously at a disadvantage. Therefore, Rostov and Kharkiv were connected to form a line, and they were held as strongholds as a starting point for the offensive in the coming spring. Therefore, according to the German authorities, the stubborn defense of the strongholds in the center of each front is not a matter of maintaining the line, and the desperate battle of the Sixth Army, which is now isolated in Stalingrad, also shows the German plan for the future of the war. The battle for Rostov is now the most critical juncture in this winter campaign. The geographical value of Rostov is of great importance to the future of the war between Germany and the Soviet Union. Especially for the Soviet army, isn't it now pouring all its elite forces into a decisive battle under the conditions of winter to defend the Volga and the Caucasus? The taste of the current stage of the war is significantly different from the situation during the Soviet counteroffensive last winter, roughly as follows:

(1) Last winter, the severe cold was another 40 degrees below zero, and the average climate in central and southern Russia this year is about 25 degrees.

(2) The Soviet Union hoped to bring all the reserve troops training in the rear together and concentrate them in the southern war zone, starting operations before the completion of the German winter front-line positions.

(3) The international situation in North Africa has changed, and a part of the military has already moved.

However, this Soviet counteroffensive was blocked by the German army's ability to defend and fight well. In a blink of an eye, the spring and summer when the front line will be active will soon arrive. At that time, the Soviet Union will be shocked by its own losses. The German authorities now frankly admit that part of the Eastern Front war situation has been lost. At the same time, the new sharp troops who have been fully prepared after General Winter and General Mud have passed are about to appear. The current Eastern Front war situation can show one end of the German authorities' determination. (Xiang: Translated from the Tokyo Mainichi Shimbun, February 1)

The Fierce and Unmatched Japanese Navy Air Force

On-the-Spot Report by American War Correspondent: Deification of Japanese Military Combat Skills - Using Ingenuity to Make Themselves Elusive - Charging into Combat and Treating Danger as Nothing

The attempt by the main force of the US military to carry out a desperate battle in the Southwest Pacific was shattered by the continuous counterattacks of the Japanese army. Throughout the United States, the magnitude of the sacrifices and the depth of the blows were shuddering, and people increasingly felt the "terror of the Japanese army." An American reporter on the front line in that area made the following report on the Japanese army's unpredictable, brave, and decisive combat in the jungle, which attracted widespread attention. The bravery of the Japanese army in the Southwest Pacific is like that of a tiger in the forest. Former Ambassador to Japan, Grew, based on his past experience, said: "The Japanese army is a formidable enemy of the United States." The Japanese army does not like to fight defensive battles but often takes the offensive. Their melee attacks, with their spirit of charging forward and never retreating, often terrify the US military, leaving them at a loss. In forest warfare, both sides are buried in piles of ancient green leaves, and the distance between the two sides is only a few feet. In such difficult and dangerous circumstances, the Japanese army skillfully uses camouflage tactics to achieve great results, often firing at the enemy from secret locations, and the enemy simply does not know where the bullets are coming from. This tactic is especially used in night battles, making it impossible for the enemy to grasp their own location, often causing illusions. Japanese soldiers often call out the names of American soldiers in a low voice, such as Smith or Brown. Infantrymen on guard duty in the forest, exhausted, actually think that their squad leader or company commander is approaching. If they are even slightly careless and answer, they are simply telling the enemy where they are, and then they are suddenly attacked. They also often hum popular American songs and sneak into American military positions. In order to prevent the enemy from noticing the sound of rubbing against trees when the troops move through the forest, the army often imitates the cries of birds and beasts, or the roar of lions, to startle and confuse the American army. Before they are even aware, the flying generals have descended from the sky. When the Japanese army moves, they are silent, as light and quiet as a raccoon dog. You can't hear a sound, and you can't see a shadow.

The Japanese army often uses a small unit to suddenly appear in front of the American army. The American army, of course, immediately starts firing, but the main force of the Japanese army, lurking to one side, unexpectedly launches a fierce attack on the American army, catching them off guard and wiping them out. The American army is also often subjected to a sudden attack directly into the heart from the front, while simultaneously encountering a deadly blow. Night raids are even more tragic. During one attack on an American position, the Japanese army first used large bombers with sun symbols on both wings to bomb the American position fiercely. Immediately, Japanese soldiers suddenly appeared from the forest, charging from both sides, shouting "Banzai," throwing grenades, and waving Japanese swords, rushing in like a raging tide. No matter how hard you try to defend, those in the back keep coming one after another. In the darkness, they engage in a desperate melee battle with grenades, pistols, and bayonets, finally breaking into a corner of the American position, starting to sweep with machine guns, and continuing the brutal fighting.

During these two days of fierce fighting, three Japanese soldiers, one of whom was an officer, suddenly jumped out of the forest, shouting "Banzai," and waving their swords, broke into the headquarters of American commander, Major General Bundacliff. The headquarters was unprepared, and this attack was completely unexpected. These three Japanese soldiers killed dozens of American soldiers, and the commander barely escaped with his life, fleeing into the depths of the forest. Because of this battle, the bravery of the Japanese army caused the entire American army to shudder. The Japanese army's equipment is extremely suitable for forest warfare. The Japanese army effectively uses mortars and other military equipment, and the exquisite mortars and grenades are very light and easy to carry. One person can carry them, and can fire the mortar after bracing it on the knee. The Japanese army also has flame throwers, and its grenades are also more powerful than those used by the American army.

The Japanese army's rifles are extremely accurate, and the grenades used to deal with the war are very powerful. The soldiers who throw them often even use themselves as human bombs, approaching tanks and detonating together. The Japanese army also has many steel boots, which they use to climb coconut trees and snipe at the enemy from above, which is extremely brave and well-trained. American commander, Major General Bundacliff, sighed and said: "If we do not abandon obsolete military tactics and adopt new tactics, there is no hope of victory." The Japanese army treats difficulties and dangers that other armies would consider impossible as nothing, and marches forward bravely. This kind of battle is still continuing fiercely. The enemy is extremely tenacious and full of confidence. It is worrying whether we can reap great results from the Japanese army in this area." (Dispatch from Kofuta, correspondent in Buenos Aires, Argentina, January 29th. Translation: Translated from the February 1st Tokyo Yomiuri Shimbun)

French Concession Revises Household Registration; Residents Must Not Conceal; Movement Must Be Reported to the Baojia Office; Violators Will Be Fined 30 Yuan

In order to thoroughly investigate and clarify the accurate number of residents in the concession and to detect any suspicious individuals, the Baojia authorities of the French Concession have decided to revise the household registration. This matter is now actively underway. Household registration forms have been distributed by the authorities in each district to the Baojia offices under their jurisdiction. After obtaining these household survey forms, residents must fill them out in detail and must not conceal, falsely report, or misreport. Furthermore, recently, the Baojia authorities have noted that residents often do not report their movement to the Baojia office, resulting in discrepancies between the household registration and the information filled in on the household registration form. In the future, if it is discovered during the revision of household registration that there has been movement of households that has not been reported to the Baojia authorities, a fine of 30 yuan will be imposed and no leniency will be granted. Residents are urged to pay attention to this.

Careful Handling of Overdrafts Between Exchange Firms; Old Customers Begin Sending Current Account Books

After the members of the Money Trade Association and the various exchange firms listed on the market, regarding the new policy for the operations of each firm, they adopted a prudent policy. For credit loans, the legitimate purpose and reliable guarantor must be explained. The collateral for goods must be limited to the goods themselves, and the term must not exceed three months. The overdraft quota must be stipulated for overdrafts, and a guarantee from a person with a good credit history is required. Recently, each firm has begun to send current account books to old customers with reliable credit, allowing them to do business. As for the interest on deposits and debts, it will be calculated in accordance with the market price announced by the association each month. It is reported that the association has scheduled a general meeting of members of each firm on February 17th at the North City Conference to celebrate the Lunar New Year. In addition to offering sacrifices to the former directors, the association will also report on matters related to business innovation.

United Relief Association of Charities, New Initiatives for Poverty Alleviation: Already Established an Almshouse and a Ciji Children's Home

In order to provide relief to orphans, widows, impoverished men, women, disabled elderly, and poor children on the streets, the Shanghai Charity Organizations Joint Relief Association, in addition to continuing to set up shelters as usual, has recently established an almshouse and a Ciji Children's Home in accordance with the principle of human mutual assistance. The reporter has learned the details and recorded them as follows:

More Than 800 Orphans, Widows, and Disabled

The almshouse is located on the site of the Tongren Fuyuan Hall Public Cemetery at the intersection of North Zhejiang Road and Qipu Road. Several sheds have been built. As of yesterday, it has taken in more than 100 elderly men and women who have no home to return to, more than 80 disabled men and women, more than 80 elderly widows, more than 200 orphans, and more than 200 extremely poor men and women, for a total of more than 800 people.

Accepting Beggar Children; Half Work, Half Study

The Ciji Children's Home is located at the same location as above and specializes in taking in beggar children from the streets. To date, it has more than 300 children. They are divided into half work and half study on weekdays, receiving half a day of adequate education and guiding the cattle in production work in order to cultivate skilled talents. With regard to the almshouse, most of the women go out to work, about 100 people, divided into sewing, picking tea leaves, and rolling cotton clothes.

Handicraft Income, Small But Helpful

Another part of the men and women work indoors, about 200 people, including more than 50 people knitting velvet yarn gloves and weaving colored wax yarn mesh bags. Each day, they can knit 60 dozen mesh bags, which are specially sold to Wing On, Sincere, New Wing On, The Sun, China National Products Company, and major stores. On average, each person can earn between 3 and 5 yuan in Central Reserve Bank notes per day. However, elderly women are unable to do manual labor and specialize in pasting tattered cloth shoe linings, which can also generate some income.

Shelters Have Six Sheds

The 11th Shelter is currently located on Alabaster Road and has six sheds. It has been open since the 1st of this month and has taken in 213 extremely poor men and women who are stranded on the streets. The cost of providing supplies is about 20,000 yuan per month, for a total cost of 40,000 yuan for the two months until the end of March, all of which is funded by the Seventh District Public Welfare Association and the Chinese Red Swastika Society.

It is reported that the association's statistics show that the monthly expenses for the almshouse and the Ciji Children's Home are about 60,000 yuan. In addition to a small subsidy from the Disease Relief Association, the shortfall is significant.

Siren Alarm Test This Afternoon

Shanghai (Central News Agency) - The Japanese Naval Fleet Headquarters in China has scheduled to test the air raid sirens this afternoon (11th) from 2:00 PM to 3:00 PM for one hour. Citizens of the city are asked to pay attention.

The Japanese authorities will test the siren alarm on the afternoon of the 11th of this month from 2:00 PM to 3:00 PM, with two long sounds lasting 12 seconds each, separated by 15 seconds. These siren sounds will continue to be rehearsed several times. It is hoped that the public will not misunderstand them as real air raid alarms.

96 Insurance Companies Registered in This City

The Ministry of Industry, in view of the recent rapid development of the insurance industry and the emergence of new companies like bamboo shoots after a rain, has specially established the National Insurance Supervision Bureau in Shanghai to protect the assets of merchants and residents. All insurance companies that are established and operating must apply to the bureau for registration and obtain a license before they are allowed to operate. Since then, new insurance companies have continued to prepare for establishment in this city in recent months. Observing the progress of the industrial and commercial promotion in Shanghai, the large number of insurance companies seems to be excessive. Therefore, the Ministry of Industry specifically issued a clear order last year to ban the registration and operation of insurance companies established after December 18th of last year. It is reported that the Insurance Supervision Bureau has now approved the registration and operation of 96 insurance companies. Recent applications for registration have been rejected.

Fruit and Vegetable Industry to Implement Rationing

In order to prevent price increases and fix prices, the fruit and vegetable industry in this city has been issued certificates by the Public Works Department and the Association Course to organize the "Fruit and Vegetable Retailers Association." According to reports from the Datong News Agency, in the future, all fruits and vegetables sold by each fruit and vegetable seller in this city will be rationed by the joint organization.

At the Reception for Reporters at the Japanese Embassy, Director-General Hanasui of the Currency Agency Gave a Talk on the Central Reserve Bank Notes; The Current Exchange Rate for Central Reserve Bank Notes and Military Scrip Remains Unchanged; Rumors of New Currency Are Pure Nonsense

The Shanghai Office of the Japanese Embassy held its customary reception for the press in this city on the 8th floor of the Cathay Hotel at 3:00 PM on the 9th. Those present included Information Director Hirota of the Embassy, Acting Director-General of the Financial Bureau Eiji Hanasui, and more than 20 reporters from various newspapers in this city. First, Mr. Hanasui gave a talk on currency issues, stating: "Currently, there are two types of currency in China, the Central Reserve Bank Notes and the Military Scrip. The exchange rate is 18 yuan in Military Scrip for 100 yuan in Central Reserve Bank Notes. This was jointly announced by Minister Zhou of Finance and Financial Officer Ohara when old currency was banned last year, stating that the exchange rate would never be changed. This has remained unchanged to this day.

No Consideration of Changing Currency

However, recently, rumors have repeatedly arisen in Shanghai, claiming that the value of Central Reserve Bank Notes may change, or that the Japanese Greater East Asia Ministry will issue Greater East Asia Securities to replace Central Reserve Bank Notes. All of these are pure nonsense. The Chinese and Japanese authorities have never considered changing the existing currency, and there is no possibility of realizing such a fact. The Chinese and Japanese authorities have already created a good foundation for the existing Central Reserve Bank Notes and have no need to issue new currency to replace them. Especially after the Greater East Asia War, not only the people in Central China will regard it as the only unified currency, but also South China and other places. After the National Government joined the war, China and Japan are fighting under the same position and the same ideals. People in both countries hope for final victory. Finance is even more important than the war. Therefore, Japan especially hopes that the Central Reserve Bank Notes can further consolidate its foundation and stabilize its circulation. Japanese Minister Aoki also clarified that 'The exchange rate between Central Reserve Bank Notes and Japanese currency will be jointly maintained by the two countries and will not be changed. In the past, the purchase of materials in various departments in China was exchanged with Military Scrip, but now it can be exchanged with Central Reserve Bank Notes, the purpose of which is to fully circulate the Central Reserve Bank Notes.' Minister Aoki was once the highest economic advisor in China, and his maintenance and consolidation of the value of the Central Reserve Bank Notes is inevitable. The rumors circulating in Shanghai can be dispelled from now on.

China and Japan Strive for Circulation of Materials

Mr. Hanasui briefly expressed his views on the issue of materials, saying: 'Although I am not directly involved in prices, I specialize in currency. Fluctuations in currency will cause riots in materials. Regarding this point, the phenomenon of material turmoil in Shanghai is actually caused by the interior. The turmoil in the interior of the guerrilla areas has affected Shanghai, causing prices to rise sharply. Enabling materials to flow smoothly in the future is the only way to stabilize prices. Recently, the National Government and the Japanese authorities have agreed to promote the mutual circulation of materials between the interior and Shanghai. It is expected that a specific plan will be announced soon. It can be expected that the agricultural production this year is unusually abundant, increasing by 30% compared with previous years. The cotton in North China has also doubled. These abundant materials can be supplied continuously, and the phenomenon of turmoil can be suppressed in the future. In addition, China can be self-sufficient in coarse grains and cotton. The lack of rice, sugar, and South Asian rubber and oil will be handled by Japan in the future to avoid the worry of shortages.' Then, Information Director Hirota made a brief report on the issue of the return of the concessions and the world situation in the past week.

Developing Enemy Property, Can Be Used

Hanasui also stated that Minister Zhou raised important issues in Shanghai: (1) to expand productivity; (2) to enrich the Central Reserve Bank Notes. The Japanese side also considers them to be important issues. Recently, Japan has returned new enemy property worth approximately 5.1 billion yuan in Central Reserve Bank Notes. China can fully utilize the recovery and management of this asset and further solve the above two major problems. He also said that due to the relationship of war, the currency of any country is showing a wartime phenomenon. But we should adopt the spirit of active construction, cherish the national currency, and protect its legal value. Do not have a critical and skeptical attitude. Then, he answered various questions raised by the reporters. At 5:30 PM, tea and refreshments were served and the meeting adjourned.

In order to care for the health of the people and ensure public sanitation, the authorities in the two concessions have successively implemented vaccination programs. The first phase of this year's flour distribution based on population in the West Shanghai district has officially begun yesterday (the 10th), with the district authorities working with more than sixty rice shops in the three neighborhoods within the district. Sino-Japanese Calligraphy Symposium

Our country has always been known as a land of culture. The evolution of Chinese characters has a history of thousands of years. From tadpole script to Great Seal script, Small Seal script, and inscriptions on bronzes, oracle bones, and stone drums, all evolved from the Seal script. After the Han Dynasty, the Clerical script flourished again. Subsequently, the Cursive script, Running script, and Regular script gradually developed with the changing times. Therefore, calligraphy is valued as a specialized academic discipline by the literati and is listed as a required subject. Moreover, writing can express a person's personality, cultivate temperament, and nurture the body and mind. Calligraphy, in particular, has a profound effect. Therefore, those who study calligraphy must undergo academic examination in order to advance. China and Japan share the same writing system, and it is necessary to study the art of calligraphy together. The Shanghai branch of the Sino-Japanese Cultural Association, recognizing this, is holding a Sino-Japanese calligraphy symposium at the Japanese-Chinese Club branch of the Cathay Hotel at 2:30 PM on the 13th of this month to promote the exchange of art between the two countries and to study calligraphy. The Chinese side has invited Wang Ge Yi, Bai Jiao, Lu Shi Qian Ji Shou Zheng, Wu Dong Mo, Zong Lu Gu Zhang Yan Chang Ma Gong Yu, Xia Jing Guan, Deng Fen Weng, and others. The Japanese side has invited Matsumura, Otani, Fujita Jyoichi, Takahashi Yasui, and about twenty others. All are well-known figures in the calligraphy world of both China and Japan.

Cause of the Fire at the "Welcoming Sun Building" in Hardoon Garden Determined; Electric Stove Boiling Water Caused Short Circuit; Luo Yunzhi Sentenced to Six Months

On the morning of the 25th of last month, at about 2:00 AM, a sudden fire broke out at the Welcoming Sun Building inside Hardoon Garden (also known as Ai Li Garden) at 1273 Jing'an Temple Road. At that time, the wind fanned the flames, making it difficult to extinguish. It was not until dawn that the fire was extinguished by the fire brigade. However, the magnificent Welcoming Sun Building was completely destroyed. Fortunately, the more than 200 residents of the entire building were alerted early enough to avoid casualties. However, the estimated losses amounted to no less than one or two million yuan. After the incident, the Jing'an Temple police station in charge ordered an investigation into the cause of the fire. It was found that Luo Lingzhi (34 years old, from Shanghai), the adopted granddaughter of the late Hardoon Garden hostess, Luo Jialing, had returned to her room after finishing a mahjong game that evening. She boiled water on an electric stove in front of her bed to make tea. However, while boiling the water, Luo talked with Nara, the eldest adopted daughter of Luo Jialing, causing the water to boil over, damaging the electric wires, and causing a short circuit, which led to the disaster. The police station believed that Luo was not without fault and should be held responsible for the crime of arson under the criminal law. Therefore, she was arrested and prosecuted by the First Special Court for the crime of arson. Yesterday, after hearing the case, the Special Court sentenced Luo Yunzhi to six months of imprisonment for arson and destruction of a residence used by people. If she chooses to pay a fine in lieu of imprisonment, it will be calculated at three yuan per day. Luo expressed her willingness to accept the sentence.

Zhao Guangfu, the Major Criminal Who Assassinated Tang Jiapeng, Dies

Zhao Guangfu, a notorious thief from Yangzhou, was 38 years old this year. He was originally a carpenter. In the summer of the 22nd year of the Republic (1933), he was instigated by others to collude with accomplices to shoot and kill Tang Jiapeng, the former manager of the Great World amusement park. He then used the gun used to kill Tang to form a gang and commit robberies, and was arrested. The Tang case was tried three times, and he was sentenced to life imprisonment. This case caused a sensation at the time. Later, Zhao was transferred to the second prison under the jurisdiction of Beixinjing to serve his sentence. During the August 13th Incident, he was transferred to the rear to serve in the military. He took the opportunity to escape back to Shanghai and continued his life of theft and robbery. He was arrested by the Public Concession police and found to be an escaped convict from the previous case. He was transferred to the Second Special District Prison by the Third High Court to continue serving his sentence. He was granted amnesty and a reduction in his sentence the year before last, and his sentence was reduced to 15 years in prison. Zhao suffered from beriberi in prison and died the other day after treatment failed. After reporting the death and conducting an examination, his wife could not be located, so the charitable organization provided for his burial.

Guidelines for Submissions to "The Economic Circle" of the Shen Bao

To meet the needs of the new era, this newspaper will launch a new section, "The Economic Circle," starting February 16th of this year; the existing commercial news will also be merged into "The Economic Circle," making it a comprehensive economic section. The main purpose is to report, discuss, explore, and promote everything in the economic sphere. We are now soliciting submissions, and the guidelines are as follows:

(1) Scope of submissions: All manuscripts related to research and discussion of economic issues, news and statistics on economic markets, whether theoretical or factual, are welcome.

(2) Submission procedures: Contributors should indicate their real name and address at the end of the manuscript and affix their seal. If it is a translation, please enclose the original text. There is no limit to the length of the manuscript, but it must be clearly written and punctuated. Please send the manuscript to the "Economic Circle" Editorial Department of the Shen Bao.

(3) Submission fees: If the manuscript is published, each character will be paid 50 to 80 yuan in Central Reserve Bank notes.

Do Not Carry More Than Two Dou of Rice Per Household; Failure to Produce a Transport Permit Will Result in Punishment

The Baojia district authorities of the two concessions, fearing that some residents may not yet be aware of the ban on transporting rice, successively notified all household heads and their families the other day not to transport more than two dou of rice on the streets. Even if it is rice for household consumption, the same rules apply. Residents who wish to transport more than two dou of rice must obtain a transport permit, otherwise they will be subject to punishment.

Rationing System for Cooking Oil to Be Implemented Within Next Week; Group Sales Method to Be Discontinued

The Cooking Oil Traders Wholesale Office has been responsible for maintaining the supply of cooking oil for residents of this city, and has always adopted a rationing system for sales. In the early stages, it was able to provide for the needs of residents. However, due to the high demand from buyers, the amount of cooking oil rationed was reduced compared to before, and some oil merchants monopolized and speculated, driving up the price of oil on the black market, resulting in a panic over cooking oil and a shortage of supply. Although the wholesale office improved the cooking oil rationing method by merging the 1,830 cooking oil retail stores in the city and dividing them into Class A and Class B sales outlets, this cooking oil panic has not been resolved. Therefore, the office has been approved by the military allocation bureau to implement a cooking oil rationing system based on population, so that every resident can purchase cooking oil, showing universality and eliminating the manipulative behavior of black market oil merchants. According to reporters' inquiries with the cooking oil wholesale office, the method of selling oil through Class A and Class B cooking oil stores previously implemented will be discontinued. Because current stocks of cooking oil have been sold out, after the subsequent batch of cooking oil is transported to Shanghai, the per capita rationing of oil can be implemented in about a week. The implementation measures for the per capita rationing of oil will be announced in the coming days.

Satisfactory Coal Ball Supply Expected to be Maintained: The Committee for Controlled Coal Rationing Annual Report

The Shanghai Municipal Council's Intelligence Department announced that, for the sake of controlling coal rationing, the Council established a Committee for Controlled Coal Rationing, consisting of six members. Two of these seats were requested to be held by representatives from the French Concession Public Works Bureau, in order to seek close cooperation between the authorities of the two concessions. Furthermore, as a result of the efforts of the committee chairman, full understanding was maintained with the Japanese authorities.

Felt Panic Last Spring: Allocated Japanese Merchants' Stored Coal

In the early part of the first half of the year, coal imports completely ceased, and the coal reserves in the two concessions were very weak. As a result of the Council's organization of coal inventory registration, it was discovered that most of the stored coal was held by users. Most of these users purchased coal for emergency use, and very few held a quantity exceeding three months' needs. At the same time, the stock held by coal merchants available for sale was almost exhausted. If users had no stored coal, they felt significant hardship. At that time, all inventory was subject to the regulations of the Council's Announcement No. 564, issued on December 9th of the previous year, which stipulated that a moving permit must be obtained before transportation was allowed. This measure enabled the Council to implement the strictest control over coal distribution.

Because "free coal" (i.e., coal sold on the market) was in short supply, quickly clearing channels and increasing supply was a critical objective. It was learned that the Japanese authorities controlled a considerable daily amount of stored coal in Pudong, and were negotiating for the continued import of new goods. The Committee therefore decided to submit the entire coal problem to the Japanese authorities for consideration, requesting them to release a portion of the Pudong stored coal to meet the urgent needs of the two concessions, and to find ways to clear channels and maintain a normal supply.

The Committee conducted a detailed investigation into the coal needs of the city, and prepared a report for the reference of the Japanese authorities. This report was submitted to the Japanese authorities on January 15th of last year. By the end of January, the Committee Chairman announced that coal had begun to be allocated to the Shanghai Electric Power Company and the Shanghai Waterworks Company. At the same time, a large portion of the coal stored by Japanese merchants had been designated for supply to the two concessions.

Improved Distribution System: Gradually Lowering Prices

In order to control the coal supply, the Chamber of Commerce and the Shanghai Japanese Coal Importers Association jointly organized a Chinese Coal Merchants Association. Those who joined the association were all giants in the coal industry. Their task was to handle all coal supplies under the direct supervision of the Japanese authorities and in close cooperation with the Council, and to effectively distribute coal according to the stipulated prices. In early March of last year, the first batch of coal was allocated through the aforementioned organizations. Since then, coal has been allocated successively and periodically, and the types of coal allocated have gradually increased. The distribution system has been improved from time to time, while improving quality and gradually lowering prices. The direct allocation of coal to large users has not encountered any obstacles. The coal allocated to these users was in accordance with the stipulated prices and equivalent quantities. However, difficulties were experienced in the allocation of coal to small commercial users and households, because a significant portion of the coal allocated in this way was transferred to brokers, and when it reached the users, it often exceeded the limited price, and the amount did not match the originally allocated amount. The Japanese authorities and the Council, recognizing this, cooperated closely to implement crackdowns and take strong measures, and the situation visibly improved.

Currently, Shanghai's coal reserves are abundant, and arrivals are also strong, sufficient to meet the needs of the two concessions.

Satisfactory Coal Ball Supply: Samples Periodically Tested

Regarding the supply of coal balls, at the end of the year before last, the Hongji coal dust stored by various coal ball factories, used to manufacture high-quality coal balls, was only enough to supply the city's needs for two months. Subsequently, the Committee found ways to sell coal dust stored by some major coal merchants to coal ball factories at reasonable prices, and urged the coal ball factories to continue to fully operate and produce goods in order to avoid a coal ball panic. They also contacted the aforementioned coal allocation organizations to continue to supply coal dust. Retail coal ball stores were ordered to register in order to closely monitor the distribution situation.

Coal balls are a necessity for cooking for Chinese residents, and are the most important of all fuels. The Committee therefore paid special attention to this important commodity. The limited price of coal balls was absolutely not changed, and coal ball users quickly reacted to situations where prices exceeded the limit. At the same time, the Coal Ball Manufacturers Association was able to maintain a high level of cooperation with the Council, so controlling the price and quality of coal balls was easier than controlling coal. There was almost no occurrence of people queuing to buy coal balls in the market, which proves that the allocation of coal balls was indeed satisfactory. The Council then issued Announcement No. 6164 on November 16th of last year, stating that no permit was required to transport coal balls.

The types and quality of raw materials obtained by various coal ball factories are inconsistent, so it is not yet possible to strictly regulate the standard quality of coal balls. However, due to the periodic testing of coal ball samples, the quality of coal balls can be maintained at a fairly good level.

Cooked Noodle Industry to Obtain Raw Noodles: Must Fulfill Promise to Sell, Cooked for Customers Only, Never Sold Outside the Store

Regarding the request by noodle shops and stalls to restore flour allocation in order to produce and sell noodles, maintain the livelihoods of workers, and facilitate the purchase of food for the poor and laborers, the Datong News Agency has learned that flour for the cooked noodle industry will be allocated to the raw noodle industry, and then the cooked noodle industry will obtain raw noodles from the raw noodle industry. This can relieve the livelihoods of workers in both industries. However, the amount of flour allocated is too small to be distributed among the industry, and they are still requesting to improve the allocation method. The fried dough sticks and pancake industry and the pancake and steamed bun industry are considering a joint flour allocation and production method due to the same membership scope in both industries, in order to improve the lives of lower-class people.

Cooked Noodle Industry Guarantee

The Shanghai Municipal Council's Material Control Office, in order to prevent the cooked noodle industry from receiving raw noodles from noodle shops and then failing to act in accordance with their promises, has printed a guarantee form to order the cooked noodle industry to fill out and submit. The letter is as follows: "To whom it may concern, due to the convenience of purchasing a large quantity of raw noodles granted to our store by your office, we hereby promise to cook all the raw noodles purchased and sell them to customers, limited to consumption within the store, and to sell them according to the prices set by the authorities. Under no circumstances will they be sold for consumption outside the store. If there is any failure to fulfill the above-mentioned promises, we will allow your office to stop the convenience of supplying a large quantity of raw noodles and revoke the business license."

Fried Dough Sticks and Pancake Industry Petition

The other day, the United Benefit Association of the pancake, noodle, and fried dough sticks industry sent Dai Ziquan and others to the Shanghai Municipal Council to continue their petition. Representative Dai Ziquan guaranteed that the members of the association would abide by the regulations set by the authorities for future operations, crack down on black market phenomena, and submit the proposed price list for pancakes, fried dough sticks, and other goods for review. The price list does not include the profits, electricity, and rent of each business. They requested the authorities to consider the good intentions of each business and increase the original cost by 20% so that each business could make a living. The Pancake and Steamed Bun Industry Association also sent representatives Zhang Guanshou, Tang Miaoquan, Wang Guisheng, and Zhang Jinsheng to the Public Association Section and Material Control Office of the Shanghai Municipal Council to petition for the early restoration of flour allocation in order to maintain the livelihoods of workers and enable the poor to purchase food.

New Shanghai Movement Discusses Scout Organization

The Shanghai Special Municipal Branch of the New National Movement Promotion Committee held its second committee meeting at 3:00 PM on the 8th in the Municipal Government Conference Room. Fifteen committee members including Shen Siliang and Hu Dunfu attended. The general director of the committee was also present. Chairman Chen, concurrently the chairman of the committee, spoke first, followed by Xi, concurrently the secretary, reporting on the committee's affairs. Then, proposals were discussed, as follows: (1) The chairman submitted for discussion a draft plan for the organization of youth groups and boy scouts in the city, signed by Xi, concurrently the secretary, in order to expedite the completion of the organization of Chinese youth groups and boy scouts according to orders, and to set March 30th of this year as the official establishment date of the team headquarters in various provinces and cities, stipulating that a grand review should be held simultaneously in various places. Resolution: Passed according to the original plan. (2) The chairman submitted for discussion a memorandum from Xi, concurrently the secretary, stating that in order to complete the first phase of the organization of city and school teams of youth groups and boy scouts in the city, and to adapt to the grand review, it is proposed to first hold a training class for instructors of youth groups and boy scouts in the city, and to propose various methods. Resolution: Sent for review. Finally, Committee Member Mo made a temporary motion: (1) In order to promote the New National Movement in the city, it is proposed to organize New National Movement Practice Groups in various organizations and groups (including public and private organizations). Resolution: Passed, and a deadline of March 30th of this year was set for the organization and establishment. (2) In order to train rural youth and establish a new foundation for rural construction, and to fulfill the mission of the New National Movement, it is proposed to organize youth groups and boy scouts in various districts of Shanghai Special Municipality. Resolution: Passed, and the proposed methods were merged with the ninth proposal for consolidation. (3) In order to compile and review various relevant teaching materials and reading materials, it is proposed to organize an Editorial and Review Committee. Resolution: Passed.

Leather Shoes: Rubber Soles to be Used Instead: Material Control Office Circular

The Shanghai Municipal Council's Material Control Office, in view of the current shortage of cowhide soles, has issued a circular to the leather shoe industry association in the city, requiring all kinds of leather shoes to use rubber soles instead, in order to reduce costs and keep prices down. The association has notified its member shoe stores to comply. It is said that leather shoes sold on the market will universally adopt rubber soles in the future.

Transfer License: Late Fee Required for Supplementary Application: 30 Yuan Fine for Overdue Applications

The deadline for landlords in the Public Concession to obtain transfer licenses for January to June of this year was set from December 14th to 23rd of last year. However, many landlords have not yet obtained the application forms. They are currently applying for supplementary applications at the Transfer License Office, No. 180 Fuzhou Road, Shanghai Municipal Council Building. In order to deter them, those who have not obtained the application forms must pay a fine of 30 yuan, and a late fee of one yuan per day of delay.

Various Banks' Reserve Funds: To be Paid at the End of the Month: At Least 10% of Deposit Amount

After the Financial Affairs Inspection Office of the Central Bank implemented the temporary measures and detailed rules for managing financial institutions and the deposit reserve system for various banks, the implementation process, after consultation with the silver and money industries, involved first paying at least 5% of the reserve funds for fixed deposits and special current deposits. Then, the reserve funds of at least 10% of the current deposits were processed. Since the reserve funds for fixed and current deposits were divided into two installments, the reserve amount of each financial institution has been based on the high or low of monthly deposits as the standard for paying the reserve funds. The reserve funds for current deposits will begin to be paid at the end of this month.

The Ministry of Finance recently stated that in order to adapt to the wartime system and establish the economy, various tax policies must be actively promoted. It has been learned that the position of Director of the Jiangsu Provincial Pig Business Special Tax Bureau has been entrusted to Fan Shuhan. Mr. Fan has already arrived in Shanghai with his entourage and will go to Jiangsu to take office soon.

World-Renowned Musician Zakharov Passes Away

The Russian musician Zakharov, the current Director of the Piano Department of the National Conservatory of Music, passed away at Hong En Hospital at the end of last month. Mr. Zakharov was a world-renowned musician who had been in China for 16 years. He had also worked at the National Conservatory of Music for 14 years. Most of China's young pianists have come from Mr. Zakharov. The news of his death was mourned by all who heard it.

Shipwreck Outside Donggou Port: The Jianghai Customs Port Affairs Section announced that the Dongya Shipping Company's tugboat Tachibana Maru has sunk in the lower reaches of the port. Its location is 338 degrees true north from the Donggou Chunting Lighthouse, about 400 feet away. All masts and chimneys are exposed above the river surface. The various signals are hung on its foremast. During the day, a green flag is hung. At night, green and white lights are hung up and down. Ships sailing near the shipwreck should proceed at an extremely slow speed.

Pufferfish Poisoning Death: Of the 107 workers who were poisoned by eating pufferfish during the Spring Festival, 17 died on the same day, and yesterday another 3,000 were declared dead. As for the other 87 poisoned people, most of them are in critical condition, except for a small number who have recovered and been discharged from the hospital.

Inscriptions and Calligraphy (1)

— Bai Jiao of Yun Jian

Mr. Bai Jiao of Yun Jian is a renowned calligrapher. His orchid paintings and seal carvings are highly praised in his time. This article is a transcript of a speech, making a fair judgment on the debate between inscriptions and calligraphy in the field of calligraphy. Its outline is sufficient to guide future generations.

The debate on inscriptions and calligraphy in calligraphy dates back to the Qianlong and Jiaqing eras. Proponents of inscriptions criticize calligraphy, while those who favor calligraphy attack inscriptions. Broadly speaking, the so-called "Inscription School," from Si Shenbo to Li Meian and Zeng Nongran, with their sawtooth edges and earthworm calligraphy, once swept the scene and dominated the so-called "Calligraphy School." But now, the tide seems to have turned again.

From the perspective of mutual attacks between those who advocate learning inscriptions and those who advocate learning calligraphy, it seems to me to be merely a dispute between worm-eaten peaches and rotten persimmons. I will explain this later. Now, let's first talk about the inscriptions and calligraphy themselves. To discuss inscriptions and calligraphy, we must first understand what is called "inscription" and what is called "calligraphy." What are the definitions and boundaries of inscriptions and calligraphy themselves?

Inscription: Setting up a stone is called an inscription; inscribing words on a stone is called an inscription. The characters on the inscription are directly written on the stone by the calligrapher and then carved. This includes various stone carvings such as commemorative inscriptions, spirit paths, epitaphs, and cliff carvings.

Calligraphy: In ancient times, there was no paper, so writing on silk was called calligraphy. Silk was difficult to preserve for a long time, so ancient calligraphy was copied and carved onto stone or wood, which was also called calligraphy. The writing and carving are indirect. This includes rubbings of letters, memorials, poetry, and so on.

Generally speaking, the categories of calligraphy are based on the style of writing: such as seal script, official script, cursive script, running script, and regular script; based on the person: such as Zhong Yao, Wang Xizhi, Ouyang Xun, and Yan Zhenqing; when the calligrapher is not specified, it is based on the dynasty: such as Xia, Shang, Zhou, Qin; based on the state: such as Qi, Lu, Chu, Hao; or based on the object: such as the San Shi Pan, Mao Gong Ding, Qi Hou Lei, Lai Zi Sun Stele, Heng Yue Stele, and Yi Ying Stele. Dividing superiority based on inscriptions and calligraphy, and dividing schools based on north and south, is a new theory in calligraphy.

Originally, the one who stirred up this great wave of "honoring inscriptions and belittling calligraphy" was An Wu Bao Shenbo; following up, promoting and fueling the flames to "honor Wei and despise Tang" was Kang Changsu of Nanhai. Both Bao and Kang were eloquent debaters. Bao wrote the "Art Boat Double Sculls," and Kang wrote the "Expanded Art Boat Double Sculls" (actually, it was only one oar). These two books had a considerable impact on the calligraphy world. However, the one who started this theory was not An Wu, but Yi Zheng Ruan Yuan. And Ruan's innovation was not without the suggestion of Wang Xuzhou's saying "Jiangnan rubbings are not as good as Hebei broken steles." Ruan was an expert in classics during the Qianlong and Jiaqing eras of the Qing Dynasty. He took it upon himself to promote scholarship wherever he went, wrote extensively, and carved books widely. He was also able to write small seal script and Han official script, which were quite impressive. He first had two articles on the North-South calligraphy schools and the North Inscription-South Calligraphy theory (Yanjing Shisan Ji, Volume 1). Scholarship in the Qing Dynasty, especially textual research, was particularly developed. At that time, ancient philology made great progress. Discovering new meanings in the characters of ancient steles, tablets, and bronze inscriptions was valuable enough to correct the classics and history. Ruan was a master of classics and paid attention to calligraphy and painting. He saw that the calligraphy of the time was confined to the Pavilion Calligraphy and the Preface to the Orchid Pavilion, especially since Emperor Qianlong liked to learn Dong Qichang's calligraphy, which was itself vulgar. And the upper echelons followed suit, and the calligraphers who were called masters specialized in elegance and beauty, with no backbone at all. It had really reached a point where it could not be tolerated. Therefore, Ruan, who took it upon himself to correct abuses and raise the spirits, thought of opening the eyes of the world and finding a way out. Thus, his two innovative theories were like giving a strong heart injection to a patient, and prescribing a croton and rhubarb medicine for the patient, causing quack doctors to look at him with new eyes. The essence of the two articles was something of textual research. It can also be said that he was very revolutionary in issuing research-based essays from a historical, geographical, and political perspective. He really had insight, and it was not for nothing. Originally, scholarship is the public property of the world. He promoted inscriptions, but his spirit was entirely a scholar's attitude of establishing a new theory in scholarship. Now, let's excerpt the arguments of the two articles to explore them.

Theory of the North-South Calligraphy Schools: "The transformation from official script to regular script, running script, and cursive script really occurred between the late Han and Wei-Jin dynasties. Later, regular script, running script, and cursive script were further divided into the North and South schools. The Eastern Jin, Song, Qi, Liang, and Chen dynasties were the Southern school; Zhao, Yan, Wei, Qi, Zhou, and Sui were the Northern school. The Southern school, from Zhong Yao, Wei Guan, Wang Xizhi, Wang Xianzhi, Wang Sengqian, etc., to Zhi Yong and Yu Shinan; the Northern school, from Zhong Yao and Wei Guan, An Jing, Cui Yue, Lu Chen, Guo Shi, Shen Fu, Yao Yuanbiao, Zhao Wenshen, Ding Daohu, etc., to Ouyang Xun and Chu Suiliang."

"The Southern school's calligraphy was not very prominent from generation to generation. It was not until the Zhenguan period of the Tang Dynasty that it became popular, but the calligraphy style of Ouyang Xun and Chu Suiliang also originated from the Northern school. Even the 'Kaicheng Stone Classics' written after the Yonghui period of the Tang Dynasty still have the remnants of the Northern school."

"The Southern school is the style of the literati of Jiangzuo, sparse and beautiful, good at letters, and often uses simple strokes. Since what is valued is biased, it has gradually reached the point where it does not recognize the legacy of seal script. In the Eastern Jin Dynasty, there were already many changes. In the subsequent Song and Qi dynasties, the so-called ancient method was completely lost."

"The Northern school is the ancient method of the Central Plains, restrained, ancient, and clumsy, good at monumental inscriptions. The legacy of Cai Yong, Wei Dan, Handan Chun, Wei Jing, Zhang Zhi, Du Du, etc., in seal script, official script, eight-part script, and cursive script, still existed until the late Sui and early Tang dynasties."

"The Northern and Southern schools are as distinct as rivers and lakes that do not mix, and even the aristocratic families do not communicate with each other. This trend still existed in the early Tang Dynasty. Emperor Taizong was originally from the North, but he only loved Wang Xizhi's calligraphy, so he was close to Yu Shinan. Wang Xizhi's calligraphy actually combined the strengths of both the North and South schools, which can be verified in the existing Wang calligraphy. For hundreds of years, the Northern school has been popular, and the common people have also used it a lot. Examining the characters commonly carved on stones and tiles at that time, they all have the calligraphy style of the Northern school in the Qi and Zhou dynasties, and there are very few like the Pavilion Calligraphy or Wang Xizhi's Southern school style. After the Pavilion Calligraphy became popular among the people, there were no more Northern school styles in steles and stone carvings."

"Wang Zhong of the Liang Dynasty was a master of the Southern school. He entered the service of the Northern Dynasty, and Emperor Gaozu of the Tang Dynasty learned his longevity, so his son Emperor Taizong also loved Wang Xizhi's calligraphy."

Central China Cotton Improvement Association Plans to Increase Cotton Production to Achieve Self-Sufficiency

The Central China Cotton Improvement Association held its fifth board meeting at the Japanese Club at 2 pm on the 9th. The attendees included President Mei, Minister of Industry (represented by You Xiaobiao, Director of the Agricultural Department of the Ministry of Industry), Chairman of the Board Tatsuo Funatsu, Managing Director Takashi Tsutsumi, and more than 20 Chinese and Japanese directors to discuss the budget and business plan for the 32nd year of the Republic of China. First, Minister Mei delivered a speech on behalf of the association, and then Chairman Funatsu reported on the business plan, briefly stating that since the establishment of the association, it has been four years, and with the sincere guidance and assistance of the Chinese and Japanese governments and related parties, the organization has been enriched, the business has been expanded, and the cotton production in Central China has been improved. During the cotton growing season last year, the weather was not very good. The harvest was poor. Moreover, due to the soaring food prices, some cotton fields were converted to food crops, so the area of cotton fields decreased, and the production tended to decline, which is deeply regrettable. However, in the areas guided by the association, the harvest increased due to the cultivation of superior seeds. Currently, due to the improved quality, the selling price is also high, and the income of farmers is higher than before. Therefore, it has made many contributions to the cotton industry economy. In order to meet the needs of the military and civilians in the Greater East Asia Co-Prosperity Sphere, it is necessary to increase the cotton production in Central China. The association is adapting to this need, expanding its organization, developing its business, and at the same time, it will work with the Cotton Industry Management Office and other related agencies. If the situation allows, it plans to popularize superior seeds to Yancheng in Jiangbei and other major cotton producing areas, encourage the improvement of cotton cultivation, and also guide wheat cultivation as an incidental measure, so that it can also contribute to the food policy. It is currently striving to increase cotton production, improve the welfare of cotton farmers, and revitalize the countryside. (Ren: Translated from the February 10th Mainland New Daily)

Japan and China Cooperate to Increase Agricultural Production; The Japanese House of Representatives Budget General Assembly; Prime Minister Tojo Answers Questions from Members

At the general meeting of the House of Representatives budget on February 2, a member asked about setting the basic policy of the food production zone in Japan, China, and Manchuria. Prime Minister Tojo replied on the spot: The permanent policy of food in Japan, China, and Manchuria is being promoted. It is not necessary to rely on the South. Cooperate with China and Manchuria throughout, and encourage agriculture so that the supply is abundant. The Japanese government is currently guiding the Chinese side to revive Chinese agriculture and stabilize the lives of Chinese farmers. The government is guiding the improvement of the technical level of Chinese farmers.

In order to revive Chinese agriculture, the Japanese government established the North China Industrial Science Research Institute in Qingdao in the 11th year of Showa (1936). It has now been moved to Beijing, with complete equipment and the world's best research institute. It can be called the root of developing Chinese industry, engaging in improving cotton seeds and raising goats. The Japanese government has provided a lot of assistance to it and has great expectations. A large number of agricultural personnel have also been dispatched. The Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry has successively selected Japanese agricultural technicians to go to provide practical guidance. This year, the Ministry of Greater East Asia has proposed an additional budget of 250,000 Japanese yen to assist Chinese agriculture, which has been passed and decided to subsidize the Central China Agricultural Assistance Association. In addition, the National Government and major national policy companies have also provided assistance in various ways, dispatching technical personnel to promote the revitalization of agricultural production in Central and North China.

Prime Minister Tojo also said: In order to achieve Chinese agriculture, the necessary fertilizers are supplied, canals are opened, water conservancy is promoted, and artesian wells are drilled in North China to benefit water sources.

In the past, Chinese agriculture's fertilizers were mainly river mud, so the fertilizer content was insufficient. Fortunately, the Yongli Chemical Industry Company in Nanjing now manufactures ammonium sulfate to make up for this deficiency. The annual output is quite large, and the fertilizer problem in Chinese agriculture has been almost solved. As for other fertilizer issues, farmers are encouraged to manufacture their own, and the results are remarkable. The largest project in developing Chinese industry is the five-year plan for North China Agricultural and Civil Engineering Projects under the General Construction Department. The main purpose is to increase agricultural productivity and achieve self-sufficiency in food in North China; and to promote water conservancy facilities in order to strengthen shipping. The planned water conservancy facilities projects are the Luan River, Ji Canal, Baiyangdian Canal, Shijin Canal, and Dongping Lake. These five areas are mostly paddy fields, so the water demand is very large. The project materials are found locally. As for the start date, the rural leisure period will be used so that farmers can help with the work. There are no obstacles to the five projects since the design.

Artesian wells are being opened everywhere, especially in Shandong Province in North China, which is promoting it more vigorously. It is planned to complete 2.3 million artesian wells from January to mid-May of this year. The China-Japan Cooperative Association and local county authorities are supervising the construction day and night. The project is progressing, and the results may exceed expectations. The Japanese government has allocated 12 million Japanese yen to subsidize its expenses. (Ren: Translated from the February 5th Mainland New Daily)
